[APPENDIX ]A.—Copper Plates, 1958-59



BOMBAY



AHMEDABAD DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/1 (page 26)
Place
Vallabh Vidyānagar.—Photograph from Prof. R.G.Tiwari. Findspot: Mandasaur.
Dynasty
Guhila of Mewar
King
Saṅga
Date
Vikrama 1576, Śaka 1441, Pausha śu. 5, Monday = 1519 A.D., December 26.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the proclamation of the abolition of certain duties, such as kāmī, bisvāki, etc. for the benefit of the inhabitants of Daśapura. Mentions Rāo Aśōkamala as the thānēdāra of Daśapura and some other officer.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/2 (page 26)
Place
Aurangābād.—Impressions of copper-plates received from Shri M.N.Desh-pande, Superintendent, South-Western Circle, Department of Archaeology (through Dr. G.S.Gai). Findspot: Nimbāḷ, Indi Taluk, Bijapur District.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Refers to the gift of certain toll-incomes in favour of the temple of Kōṭiśaṅkaradēva of Nimbahaḷḷa by the Five-Hundred Svāmins of Ayyāvaḷe together with the other trade guilds and commercial bodies. In characters of about the 12th century.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/3 (page 26)
Place
Do. Findspot: Do.
Dynasty
Kalachuri of Kalyāṇa
King
Saṅkamadēva
Date
Parābhava, Mārga-śira śu. 5, Monday, Bharaṇi = 1186 A.D., November 17.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the gift of the village of Bobbula-vaddhe in Aṅkulla-ge-50 included in Tarikāḍa-kaṁpaṇa for the benefit of the temple of Kōṭiliṅgēśvara at Nimbahura. See Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 227 ff.


BARODA DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/4 (page 26)
Place
Baroda.—Shri S.R.Rao, Officer on Special duty, Department of Archaeo-logy. Through Dr. B.Ch.Chhabra, Joint Director General of Archaeology in India, New Delhi.
Dynasty
Chaulukya of Lāṭa
King
Trilōchanapāla
Date
Śaka 972, Vikṛita, Pausha śu. 9, Mon-day = 1050 A.D., December 24, f.d.t. ·17.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the gift of the village E1kallahāra situated in Karmānta-pura-116 by the king to the Brāhmaṇa Tārāditya who belonged to the Bhāradvāja gōtra and Āṅgirasa, Bārhaspatya, and Bhāradvāja pravaras and who was a sthānika of Rōhiḍa-mahāsthāna. The charter was drafted by the Mahāsāndhi-vigrahika Śaṁkara.


MADHYA PRADESH



BILASPUR DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/5 (page 26)
Place
Bilāspur.—Shri Amarnath Rao of Juni Basti. Findspot: Mallār, Bilaspur District.
Dynasty
Śarabhapurīya
King
Mahā-Jayarāja
Date
Year 5, Kārttika 5
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Box-headed
Remarks
Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIII, pp. 155 ff.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/6 (page 26)
Place
Mallār.—Impressions from Shri Bal-chandra Jain, Assistant Curator, M.G.M. Museum, Raipur.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Pravararāja I
Date
Year 41, Pausha 27
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern Nail-headed
Remarks
Issued from Prasannapura. Records the grant of the village Kūnturapadraka situated in Pūrva-rāshṭra, to the Brāh-maṇa Agnichandrasvämin, son of Durgasvāmin of the Kāpy-Āṅgirasa gōtra by Vyāghrarāja, the younger brother of the ruling king. Probably engraved by Jyēshṭhasiṁha. Pub-lished in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 45 ff.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/7 (page 26)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Pravararāja II
Date
Year 3, Pausha 2
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Box-headed
Remarks
Issued from Śrīpura. Records the gift of the village Mitra-grāma situated in Śaṅkhachakra-bhōga to Brāhmaṇa Śubha-chandra, son of Dāmōdaragaṇa of the Bhāradvāja gōtra. The engraver was Gōlasiṁha. Ibid., pp. 53 ff.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/8 (page 27)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Mahā-Jayrāja
Date
Year 9, Jyēshṭha 5
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Box-headed
Remarks
Issued from Śarabhapura. Records the gift of the village Mōkkēppikā in Nagarōttarapaṭṭa to two Brāhmaṇas named Mahīśvarasvāmin and Rudrasvāmin of the Bhārgava gōtra by Śabarabhōgika-Vatsa. The engraver was Achala-siṁha. Ibid., pp. 28 ff.


DHAR DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/9 (page 27)
Place
Dhār.—Impressions received from Sri R.B. Deshpande. Findspot: Mān-dhātā, Nimar District.
Dynasty
Paramāra of Mālava
King
Jayasiṁha-Jayavarman
Date
Vikrama 1331, Pra-māthin, Bhādra-pada śu. 7, Maitra (Anurādhā), Fri-day = 1274 A.D., August 10.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records a grant of 4 villages, Kumbhaḍāuda-grāma, Vālauda-grāma, Vaghaḍi-grāma and Nāṭiya-grāma in favour of a number of Brāhmaṇas residing in the Brahmapurī at Māndhātṛi and belonging to various gōtras and śākhās whose families hailed from several localities. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 138 ff.


MADRAS



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/10 (page 27)
Place
Madras.—Shri S.Rajam, Murray and Co., Madras. Through Shri T.N.Subra-maniam, Madras. Findspot: Paḷḷaṅ-kōvil, Tanjore District.
Dynasty
Pallava
King
Siṁhavarman
Date
Year 6
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Tamil, Grantha & Tamil
Remarks
Records the grant of the village of Amaṇśērkkai in Perunagar-nāḍu in Veṇkuṉṟakkōṭṭam and land in Tāmar to Vajranandi-kkuravar of Parutti-kkuṉṟu as paḷḷichchandam. Narabhaya, the minister, figures as the ājñapti of the grant. Published in Trans. of the Arch. Soc. of South India, 1958-59, pp. 41 ff.

TIRUNELVELI DISTRICT



KOILPATTI TALUK



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/13 (page 27)
Place
Pāṇḍavarmaṅgalam.—Impressions from the Superintendent, Government Museum. Madras.
Dynasty
Chōḷa-pāṇḍya
King
[Jaṭāvarmaṉ]Sundara-Chōḷapāṇḍya
Date
Year 10
Language & Alphabet
Tamil
Remarks
Incomplete. Seems to record the gift of the village of Pāṇḍa-varmaṅgalam alias Pañchavaṉmādēvi-chaturvēdimaṅgalam in Veṅbaikkuḍi-nāḍu to several Brāhmaṇas.
ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/14 (page 27)
Place
Tirunelvēli.—Dalavay Mudaliar. Through Shri P.K.Arunachala Gounder, Professor of Tamil, The M.D.T.Hindu College, Pēṭṭai and Shri T.N.Subra-maniam, Madras.
Dynasty
Pāṇḍya
King
Parāntakaṉ Vīranārāyaṇaṉ
Date
Year 45
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Tamil, Grantha & Vaṭṭeḻuttu
Remarks
Issued from Kaḷakkuḍi. States that while king Varaguṇa, son of Śrīmāra-Śrīvallabha, who was devoted to god Śiva, was ruling, two villages, Tirumaṅgalam and Śomāśikuṟichchi clubbed together into one were granted by the king (Parān-takaṉ-Vīranārāyaṇaṉ) to several Brāhmaṇas at the instance of Nārāyaṇaṉ-Kēśavaṉ, a learned Brāhmaṇa of Tirumaṅgalam. States also that Kaḍuṅgōṉ, a predecessor of the king, who uprooted the Kaḷappālar had granted the former of the two villages to 12 Brāhmaṇas and the latter to Kāṭhaka-sōmayājin and that subsequently the latter village was occupied by Kaḍattirukkai-kiḻavaṉ. Cf. Tamil text published in Tamiḻ Poḻil, Vol. XXXV p. 13.


ORISSA



CUTTACK DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/15 (page 28)
Place
Cuttack.—Dr. N.K.Sahu, Lecturer, Ravenshaw College. Findspot: Taicher, Dhenkanal District.
Dynasty
Tuṅga of Yamagarta
King
Gayāḍatuṅga
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit (corrupt), East Indian
Remarks
Issued from Jayapurakōṭṭa. Records the gift of the village of Svalpa-Kōmpai in the Khembāi vishaya in favour of Bhaṭṭa Bhāinādēva, son of Gōkuladēva, grandson of Bhaṭṭa Vāsudēva and who belonged to the Jatukarṇa gōtra, Vasishtha pravara, Chhandōga charaṇa and Kauthuma sakhā for the merit of the donor and his parents. The donee is said to have hailed from a Traividya (i.e. Trivēdin) family residing at a place called Śrī-chhātra. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 95 ff.


RAJASTHAN



SIROHI DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/16 (page 28)
Place
Rōhērā.—Impressions through Prof. Sadhuram, Delhi.
Dynasty
Paramāra of Ābū
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet

Remarks
The record is incomplete and the impression relates to the inner side of the first plate of a grant made by some Paramāra ruler of Arbuda (Ābu), giving a complete genealogy of the Paramāra rulers of Ābu from Utpalarāja to Dhārāvarsha. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 135 ff.


UTTAR PRADESH



LUCKNOW DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/A/1958-1959/17 (page 28)
Place
Lucknow.—Impression from the State Museum, Lucknow. Through Shri V.N. Srivastava, Assistant Curator, Archaeo-logical Museum, Mathurā.

Gāhaḍavāla

Vijayachandra

Vikrama 1221, Phāl-guna, śu. 7, Friday, Rōhiṇī = 1165 A.D., February 19.

Records the grant of the village Kanhavarā in Valai-pattalā to Ṭhakkura Narasiṁha of Vāsisht6ha gōtra by the king. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 223 ff.

Place

Kākatīya
King
Gaṇapati
Date
(1) Śaka 1124 (Jina-Bhava), Duṁdubhi, Tapasya (i.e. Phāl-guṇa), Saptamī. (2) Śaka 1127-(ṛiksha-bhūmi-iṁdu), Krōdh-ana, Māgha, rākā-dina, śu. 15 = 1206 A.D., January 26.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Telugu

Records the consecration of the deities Aitēśvara on the former date and Annēśvara and Mallikārjuna on the latter and grants of land and flower garden made to the same by Mailama.

Place

Do.

Trailōkyamalla (Sōmēśvara I)
Date
Śaka 969, Sarvajit, Vaiśākha śu. 3, Wednesday = 1047 A.D., April 1.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Gives the genealogy of the Chālukya family upto Trailōkya-malla and introduces a subordinate chief, Daṇḍanāyaka Nāgavarma of the Vāji family, whose genealogy also is given. Worn out. Records gifts of lands, garden and oil-mill to the gods Svayaṁbhu-Sōmanātha and others. Siṁgamayya wrote the record and Kētōja of Abbalur engraved it.

Date

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records that when Siṁgeya-daṇṇāyaka, the Mahāpradhāna of the Hoysaḷa kingdom, raided Haṇaje in the Eḍaveṭṭa country and drove away the cattle, Nāḷaprabhu Sāvanta Kāḷagauḍa of Mējūr, disciple (?) of Mūṟujāvidēva, attacked him near the border of Jiḍugūr and Vonnāli (i.e. Honnāḷi) and died in the fight that ensued after freeing the cattle. The record states that Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kumāra Bommi-dēvarasa was administering the country from his capital at Hosaguda.

ARIE/1958-1959/B/1958-1959/590 (page 85)
Place
Another slab in the same place
Dynasty
Do.
King
Bijjala
Date
Śaka 1087, Pārthiva, Uttarāyaṇa saṁkrā-nti lunar eclipse. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Worn out at the top. Records a gift of income from several taxes by Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Īśvaradēva of the Sinda family of Beḷagutti, to god Mallikārjuna whose temple at Niḍu-nēgila was built by Ūroḍeya Mahādēva. The record gives genealogical account of the donor. It also registers the grant of land, garden, oil-mill and income from taxes, to the same god, for worship and offerings as also for feeding the ascetics and students, by Ūroḍeya Mahādēvaṇṇa with the permission of Īśvaradēva, and Barmayya, the Daṇḍanāyaka of the mēlāḷike of Banavāsi-12000. The gift was made over to the āchārya of Dakshiṇa-Kēdārēśvara of Balipura. The latter is said to have been administering a vast area, the details of which are enumerated, from his capital at Haḷavura.

ARIE/1958-1959/B/1958-1959/607 (page 87)
Place
Slab set up by the side of the same temple
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vijayāditya (Bijjaḷa)
Date
(1) Jagadēkamalla year...., [Śaka] 1070, Prabhava, Paushya Amāvāsye, Uttarāyaṇa-saṁ-krānti, Monday. = 1174 A.D., Decem-ber 24, Wednesday. The Śaka year was current. (2) Sarvajit, Chaitra puṇṇami, Vishu-saṁkramaṇa, Monday. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records that Kāma-gāvuṇḍa, son of Kētiseṭṭi had the temple of Rāmēśvara built at Emmanūr situated in Nāgarakhaṇḍa of Banavāse-nāḍu, and donated a garden and land to the same on the first date. On the same day the Five hundred (mahājanas) of the place and also Mallibōva-daṇḍanāyaka, an officer in charge of the taxes donated the income from the taxes. In the next year, Vibhava, Kāmagāvuṇḍa having passed away, his son Rēcha-gāvuṇḍa renewed the same gifts and entrusted them into the hands of Aṭṭa-hāsa-muni of the Pāśupata school on the second date. The inscribed slab was set up by Masaṇi-seṭṭi, son of Jakki-seṭṭi. At the time of the second date Sōvidēva of the Kadamba family was governing the Banavase country. Cf. M.A.R, 1928, p. 77, No. 79.

Place

Do.

Śaka 976, Jaya, Pushya, Uttarā-yaṇa-saṁkrānti. Probably = 1054 A.D., December 24, Saturday.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the installation of the god Maḷibēśvara by Māḷiyabbarasi, wife of Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Rēvarasa and registers a grant of land by her for the worship of the god, the maintenance of musicians and feeding of ascetics and students studying in the maṭha. Keṁbāvi is described as Rājadhāni. The record was written by Chaṅgadēvayya. Rēvarasa is credited with subduing Mummuṇi Koṅkaṇiga. Noticed in Ep. Ind., Vol. XII, pp. 292-93.

RAICHUR DISTRICT



DEVADURG TALUK



ARIE/1958-1959/B/1958-1959/661 (page 92)
Place
Gabbūr.—Slab set up near the Baṅgārada Basavaṇṇa temple.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa
King
Tribhuvanamalla [Vikramāditya VI]
Date
Chālukya-Vikrama year 20, Yuva, Pushya ba. 11, Mon-day, Uttarāyaṇa-saṁkrānti = 1095 A.D., December 24, f.d.t. ·42.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records a grant of land by Sarvakratu Eṟeyaṇa-bhaṭṭōpā-dhyāya Sōmayāji to the gods Vishṇudēva, Rāmēśvaradēva and another (name lost). The donor had received this land as one of the Two Hundred (mahājanas) who were the recipients of the villages Hūvinahāḷu and Kalmale from the king. Also states that the village Gobbūr was given by Āhavamalla to the mahājanas as dakshiṇā at the time of the performance of kōṭi-hōma.

BAIBAT TAHSIL



ARIE/1958-1959/B/1958-1959/762 (page 101)
Place
Bairāṭ.—Slab fixed into the wall of the Jain temple.
Dynasty
Timurid
King
Jalāla[dīna] Akabbara, son of Humāun
Date
[Vikrama 1644 ?], Śaka 1509, Phāl-guna śu. 2, [Sun-day] = 1588 A.D., February 18.
Language & Alphabet
Local dialect, Nāgarī
Remarks
Damaged and fragmentary. Begins with an adoration to guru Hiravijaya-sūri. Mentions Bhāramalla who received the governorship of many villages from the Pātaśāha's subordinate Ṭōḍaramalla and Bhāramalla's son Indrarāja who received the governorship of Vaīraṭa-draṅga and his brother Ajayarāja. Indrarāja built the temple of Vimalanātha called Mahōdaya-prāsāda and also Indra-vihāra and installed many images including those of Pārśvanātha, Chandraprabha and Ṛisha-bhadēva bearing the names of his father, himself and his brother respectively. Akbar is mentioned as worshipped by the fourteen Chhatrapatis and numerous Maṇḍalādhipatis and also apparently as the lord of the maṇḍalas of Kaśmīra, Kāmarūpa,..tāna (probably Mūlatāna), Kābila (Kabul), Bada-kaśā (Badakshān), Ḍhillī, Marusthalī, Gurjjaratrā, Mālava, etc. The record described as Indra-vihāra-prāsāda-praśasti, was composed by Paṁ. (i.e. Paṇḍita) Lābhavijaya-gaṇi and was written on the stone by Paṁ. Sōmakuśala-gaṇi. Also mentions Mahōpādhyāya Kalyāṇavijaya-gaṇi. Probably engraved by Musarapha, Bhagarū and Mahamadāla, sons of Bhairava. Cf. Bhandarkar's List, No. 810; PRAS., W.C., 1909-10 p. 45.

LUCKNOW DISTRICT



ARIE/1958-1959/C/1945-1946/422 (page 114)
Place
Lucknow.—Provincial Museum. Slab. Findspot: Fort wall at Mahōbā, Hamirpur District.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Vikrama 1240, Āshāḍha ba. 9, Monday = 1184 A.D., June 4. (The year was Kārttikādi and the month Pūrṇimānta).
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit (verse), Nāgarī
Remarks
Fragmentary. Records the construction of a Śiva temple by the ruler (name lost) who belonged to the lunar race. The temple was caused to be constructed by the Brāhmaṇa, Mādhava. The praśasti was composed by Jayapāla of the Vāstavya family and engraved by Dēvarāja, son of Sōmarāja. Published in Bhārata Kaumudī, Part I, pp. 433 ff., and Plate.
